width="auto"><div class="stMarkdown" data-testid="stMarkdown"><div data-testid="stMarkdownContainer" class="st-emotion-cache-1104ytp e1icttdg0"><p>UNIT SIX: SPECIAL HEALTH ISSUES</p>
<p>In this unit you will cover provision of health services for special groups of people.</p>
<p>This unit is composed of 4 sections:
Section One: Individuals and Groups with Special Health Needs.
Section Two: Disaster Management.
Section Three: School Health Programmes.
Section Four: Occupational Health Services.</p>
<p>Unit Objectives</p>
<p>By the end of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Identify individuals/groups who need special health services in the community and take appropriate action</li>
<li>Mobilise and sensitise the community to respond appropriately in emergencies and disease outbreaks</li>
<li>Manage school health programmes</li>
<li>Identify occupational health hazards in the community and take appropriate action</li>
</ul>
<p>SECTION 1: INDIVIDUALS AND GROUPS WITH SPECIAL HEALTH NEEDS</p>
<p>Introduction</p>
<p>In this section you will look at individuals and groups with special health needs. You will also look at the needs of people with hearing and visual impairment, children in need, the elderly, chronically ill patients, displaced persons, widows and widowers.</p>
<p>Objectives</p>
<p>By the end of this section you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define the term disability</li>
<li>Identify and manage individuals and groups in need of special health services</li>
<li>Describe services available for people with special health needs</li>
</ul>
<p>Definition of Disability</p>
<p>In life anything that stops a part of your body from functioning fully is known as impairment.</p>
<p>There are many different types of impairments such as motor, sensory, and emotional or intellectual impairment.</p>
<p>How you would define the term 'disability'</p>
<p>A disability is a physical, emotional or mental injury or illness that is severe or permanent, that interferes with an individual's normal growth, development or ability to learn or work.</p>
<p>In this section you will see the words disability and impairment used interchangeably. Most disabilities start at birth or in childhood. Those that start later in life are often as a result of accidental injury. In many cases the loss of a function due to disability need not make a person useless.</p>
<p>Often disabled people have other faculties which they can put into good use and therefore be able to earn a living for themselves and their family. For example, blind people can work as telephone operators, those with disabilities affecting the legs can do any work that requires the use of their hands. In order to help them you will identify their abilities and modify the environment to avoid overtaxing them. You will also provide them with appliances and the appropriate apparatus, in order to develop their potential ability and compensate for the defect.</p>
<p>Types of Disabilities</p>
<p>List down various types of disabilities that are common in the community you serve.</p>
<p>The following are types of common disabilities:</p>
<p>Physical Disabilities</p>
<p>These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Motor defects due to congenital causes such as missing limbs, trauma, cerebral palsy (spastics).</li>
<li>Sensory defects such as blindness and deafness.</li>
<li>Chronic illness, for example, epilepsy.</li>
</ul>
<p>Mental Disability</p>
<p>Due to mental deficiency, these include: mongolism, birth injuries, meningitis and emotional problems.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 181 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>You will consider two types of impairments, namely hearing and visual impairment. You will also learn their causes, management, and services available for people with these impairments and how they can be prevented.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hearing-impairment">Hearing Impairment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hearing-impairment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-is-hearing-impairment">What is hearing impairment?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-hearing-impairment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Hearing impairment is a disability that hinders successful processing of sound waves through audition, that is the inability to hear or interpret/perceive sound waves.</p>
<p>Hearing impairment is classified according to the units used to measure the loudness of sound. These units are known as decibels (db). Human contacts and relationships depend on communication by means of speech. A person who has profound hearing impairment cannot converse with others unless they can both use and understand sign language.</p>
<p>Impairment in hearing may also cause changes in personality and attitude, awareness of the surroundings and ability to protect oneself. This calls for a great deal of patience and tolerance from other people when dealing with the patient. People with hearing impairment try to conceal their disability by developing some defence mechanisms, such as withdrawing from contact with others and displaying unreasonable irritability and aggressiveness.</p>
<p>It is therefore important for health workers to bear this in mind as they help a person with hearing impairment. Sometimes the person may even reject the help required to facilitate their hearing.</p>
<p>For example, they may refuse to wear hearing aids because they feel it advertises their disability.</p>
<p>It is therefore important to teach family members and the community how to cope and live with a person who has hearing impairment. This is better than educating or training anyone with moderate hearing impairment.</p>
<p>There are two terms used to describe hearing impairment, which are based on time of onset of hearing loss and the functional status of hearing. These are total hearing loss and hard of hearing. You will now look at what each means.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="total-hearing-loss-deafness">Total Hearing Loss (Deafness)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#total-hearing-loss-deafness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A person who is born completely deaf and who in the past has never developed speech is described as deaf and dumb (Davies, B.M, 1978).</p>
<p>This person has total hearing loss and the sense of hearing is non functional for ordinary purpose of life. The person is dumb not due to a defect in voice production but because normal speech is only learnt by copying what is heard.</p>
<p>Deafness is classified into:</p>
<ul>
<li>Congenital deafness, which is loss of hearing before speech is developed.</li>
<li>Adventitious deafness, which is when one is born with normal hearing, but later suffers some illness or accident causing the hearing to become non functional.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="hard-of-hearing">'Hard of Hearing'<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hard-of-hearing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>'Hard of Hearing' is the term used to describe a person who although has defective hearing, it is serviceable with or without hearing aids.</p>
<p>This term indicates that although the person is deaf the person has normal speech.</p>
<p>Examples are people with:</p>
<ul>
<li>Conductive hearing loss</li>
<li>Sensory hearing loss</li>
<li>Psychogenic hearing loss</li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260117-6eb35ed4.jpeg" alt="img-0.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="causes-of-hearing-impairment">Causes of Hearing Impairment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes-of-hearing-impairment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-are-the-causes-of-hearing-impairment-middle-ear">What are the causes of hearing impairment? Middle Ear<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-causes-of-hearing-impairment-middle-ear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Diseases or defects that may affect or damage the middle Include</p>
<ul>
<li>Tubal catarrh, which is the occurrence of the middle ear being permanently under pressure due to malfunctions of the eustachian tube.</li>
<li>Acute middle ear infections.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 182 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Chronic otitis media which is caused by excessive growth of the cranial bone, thus leaving little room for the ossicular chain (which is malleus, incus and stapes) to operate in. These fail to transmit sound vibrations to the inner ear leading to considerable hearing loss.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="inner-ear">Inner Ear<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#inner-ear" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The diseases and defects of the inner ear are the most serious contributors to hearing loss. They affect both perception and the recording of the four parameters of sound loudness, that is, pitch, quality and duration. These may cause other problems apart from serious hearing loss. Causes of hearing loss in the inner ear include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Congenital causes due to infections in utero such as german measles or rubella, cytomegalovirus, syphilis.</li>
<li>Brain damage especially intracranial injury in cases of difficult labour and delivery.</li>
<li>Neonatal jaundice due to hyperbilirubinemia which can lead to kernicterus. Kernicterus causes brain damage thus interfering with interpretation of the sound wave.</li>
<li>Acoustic trauma caused by loud environmental noise, which distorts the tympanic membrane making it unable to vibrate.</li>
<li>Minieres disease which causes a considerable loss of frequency analysis.</li>
<li>Postnatal incidentals, such as infections due to measles, mumps and meningitis, and the overuse of drugs such as aminoglycosides (especially neomycin), quinine, or salicylates.</li>
<li>Tumours of the auditory nerve such as acoustic neuroma.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="resources-available-for-the-hearing-impaired">Resources Available for the Hearing Impaired<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#resources-available-for-the-hearing-impaired" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="what-services-are-available-for-the-hearing-impaired-in-your-community">What services are available for the hearing impaired in your community?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-services-are-available-for-the-hearing-impaired-in-your-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Community teachers, family, institutions, special schools and associations are some available resources for the hearing impaired. In most communities it is possible to find people who have hearing impairment and who can be requested to mentor and train a child with hearing impairment. It is important to identify and use such persons because they relate easily to the emotions and difficulties the child may be going through. Some may even be trained which would be an added bonus.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="other-families-with-hearing-impaired-members">Other Families with Hearing Impaired Members<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-families-with-hearing-impaired-members" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Families with children who have hearing impairment in the same community can come together and form a support group where they share experiences. This serves as group therapy and they learn very well as a group. As a community nurse you can again motivate these families to come together and support each other, as well as support them with information and ideas about prevention, and the different services available for their children.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="institutions-for-the-hearing-impaired">Institutions for the Hearing Impaired<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#institutions-for-the-hearing-impaired" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are a number of institutions where special education and programmes for the persons with hearing loss take place.</p>
<p>You can find these through the ministry of education in our country and refer our patients to them.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="special-schools">Special Schools<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#special-schools" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Persons with hearing impairment need special training in special schools where they can learn. In our country there are many schools for persons with hearing impairment.</p>
<p>They assist them to develop skills that make them feel important and useful members of the community. Special schools are largely public institutions run like any other school. Visiting these special schools helps us to understand and appreciate their services to persons with hearing loss.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="associations">Associations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#associations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In many countries, persons with hearing impairment have formed associations to look after their needs and welfare. Some of them meet to discuss issues affecting them, and arrange for short training courses in communication skills.</p>
<p>The Kenya National Association for the Deaf advocates for the deaf to have equal access to public services such as schools and hospitals.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 183 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>They also have a job placement activity which helps deaf persons get employment as well as start income generating activities, such as small enterprises of fishing, carpet making, carpentry, sweater making amongst others.</p>
<p>Another NGO known as the Kenya National Deaf HIV/AIDS Education Programme is involved in the reduction of stigma among deaf persons affected and infected by the virus, establishment of deaf-friendly VCT sites, and development of materials for the deaf.</p>
<p>As a health worker it is important for you to know about these associations so that you can refer your patients appropriately.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-hearing-impairment">Management of Hearing Impairment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-hearing-impairment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The effective management of hearing impairment is based on early detection. It is important that you remember that in most cases impairment starts in childhood. Therefore you should ensure that all under fives are properly managed in order to prevent diseases that cause hearing impairment. The management of hearing impairment starts with assessment which then leads to the choice of an appropriate treatment option, such as surgery, hearing aid, or ear syringing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-does-assessment-mean">What does assessment mean?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-does-assessment-mean" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Assessment is the process of identifying persons with impairment and quantifying it through reliable tests. In the case of hearing impairment assessment tests are carried out by an audiologist.</p>
<p>Once the problem is diagnosed and the cause and degree of hearing loss is established, then a number of treatment options can be applied depending on diagnosis. However, the process of managing hearing problems starts right from your well-baby clinic, where children under five years of age come for treatment of ear infections, or diseases such as otitis media.</p>
<p>Screening tests also need to be carried out routinely on all the under fives to diagnose and assess if impairment exists. If this is done a child who has hearing loss or a hearing problem will be identified early and treated.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="surgery">Surgery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This can be performed if the hearing loss is not congenital. Operations can be performed on the tympanic membrane and the ossicles (malleus, incus and stapes).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ear-syringing">Ear Syringing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ear-syringing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Ear syringing may be done in cases where the hearing problem is due to excessive wax and there is no ear infection. This is mainly in the external ear.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hearing-aid">Hearing Aid<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hearing-aid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These appliances are used to correct the hearing defect in cases of mild and moderate hearing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="alternative-communication-skills">Alternative Communication Skills<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alternative-communication-skills" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is known that the development of speech reaches its peak during the first three to four years and that the optimum period for development of hearing is during the first year.</p>
<p>To give a child with hearing loss a chance to learn words and language, you should advise the parents to train them from an early age.</p>
<p>The child is taught:</p>
<ul>
<li>Lip reading to help in communication</li>
<li>Gestures or actions of the body to express issues</li>
<li>Sign language</li>
<li>Integration and rehabilitation</li>
</ul>
<p>The integration and management of hearing impaired persons should start at home and involve the whole community. This means encouraging the deaf to manage better at home and work in the community.</p>
<p>In the home you need to encourage and educate the family on how to support and live with a hearing impaired person. You should try to introduce them to other families who share the same problem in order to relieve their fears and promote acceptance of the person with hearing loss.</p>
<p>Your role and that of other health workers will be to support the family and the community by providing them with information, equipment and training.</p>
<p>Above all they will also need encouragement to strengthen social integration of the person with hearing impairment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-hearing-impairment">Prevention of Hearing Impairment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-hearing-impairment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>List two ways of preventing hearing impairment.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 184 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Your answer should have included any two of these:</p>
<ul>
<li>Prenatal labour and delivery services need to be improved to prevent occurrence of hearing impairment. Pregnant mothers should be vaccinated against german measles (rubella). The mother should also be advised to avoid taking drugs unless prescribed by the doctor. She should also have her blood checked for rhesus negative status which brings about rhesus incompatibility. Since deafness can also be caused by complications of labour and delivery, it is very important that you identify early and manage mothers who may present with labour complications. Early diagnosis is very important in order to minimise chances of intracranial injury to the newborn.</li>
<li>Early diagnosis and treatment of infections and trauma such as otitis media, ear discharge or a foreign body in the ear is very important, so as to prevent complications which may lead to hearing impairment.</li>
<li>The community should be educated on the importance of identifying these signs and seeking prompt medical advice.</li>
<li>Avoid drugs which may cause ototoxicity, or use them under medical supervision.</li>
<li>Avoid excessive noise, which may result to temporally or permanent hearing loss.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="visual-impairment">Visual Impairment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#visual-impairment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Visual impairment is the lack or inability to see, which may be caused by diseases or injuries to the eye.</p>
<p>Clarity of vision is called visual acuity and ranges from full vision to no vision.</p>
<p>Visual impairment is a fairly common impairment in our country which needs specialised medical care.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="think-about-possible-causes-of-visual-impairment">Think about possible causes of visual impairment.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#think-about-possible-causes-of-visual-impairment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following are possible causes of visual impairment:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Trachoma.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vitamin A deficiency.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Allergy.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cataract.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Macula degeneration.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Some types of cancer such as retinoblastoma and pituitary gland tumours.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Glaucoma.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Childhood blindness, for example, congenital cataract and corneal blindness.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Diabetic retinopathy.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Disorders of the nervous system such as multiple sclerosis and stroke.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Refractive errors.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ocular complications of HIV/AIDS.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Accidents which cause injury to the eye.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="services-available-for-the-visually-impaired">Services Available for the Visually Impaired<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#services-available-for-the-visually-impaired" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="at-the-family-level">At the Family Level<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#at-the-family-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Normally, activities of daily living such as feeding, socialising, playing, verbal skills, and mobility are learnt at home. A normal child learns how to do every day activities by watching what others are doing and imitating them.</p>
<p>If a child is under five years of age and is visually impaired, then they need special help from the family in order to learn these skills.</p>
<p>The family needs to train the child to recognise common domestic objects by touching. They need to provide the child with toys to play with in a room that does not put the child at risk from accidents.</p>
<p>Parents also need to be educated about the importance of keeping the child's articles and toys in their regular places, so that they can find them easily.</p>
<p>Children who are visually impaired also need more body contact, especially when talking to them to facilitate communication.</p>
<p>When the child is old enough to attend nursery school, the family should recite nursery rhymes and songs with the child, in order to prepare the child for integration into the community, where they will identify with the learning activities of other nursery school children.</p>
<p>Encourage a person who is visually challenged to have contacts relatives and friends to be contactable when the need arises. The family needs to modify the environment to prevent accidents.</p>
<p>Encourage the person to participate in activities they can perform and enjoy.</p>
<p>Your role is important in providing support and encouragement</p>
<p>to the family and availing them with information on the available resources.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 185 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 186 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="institutional-level">Institutional Level<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#institutional-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are a number of educational institutions and associations that care for visually impaired persons.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="education-institutions-schools-for-the-blind">Education Institutions: Schools for the Blind<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#education-institutions-schools-for-the-blind" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These are special schools that provide special services to the visually impaired. Some of these schools are owned and managed by the government. Others are owned and managed by non-governmental organisations and missions.</p>
<p>You should be able to identify some of these schools in your catchment area. It is beneficial for you to visit them in order to know what they do.</p>
<p>In these schools the visually impaired are taught braille, a system of reading specially developed for blind people which uses small raised marks that they feel with their fingers. Visually impaired persons can start learning from the age of five years.</p>
<p>Braille is also taught to all persons under the age of 50 years who have been blinded after enjoying good sight for many years.</p>
<p>For example, the victims of the 1998 August terrorist bomb blast in Nairobi who lost their sight were trained on how to read braille depending on their occupation. After learning how to use braille, visually impaired persons are able to pursue their studies and careers up to the university level, becoming lawyers, administrators and teachers in society.</p>
<p>In addition, they are taught survival skills and skills of daily living, such as how to get around from point A to B using a cane. Special schools play a very big role in increasing their participation in the community and facilitating their integration.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="educational-assessment-and-resources-centres-earcs">Educational Assessment and Resources Centres (EARCs)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#educational-assessment-and-resources-centres-earcs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These are centres which were created countrywide to offer assessment and referral, as well as placement of children in schools which are nearest to their homes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cbos-ngos-collaborators">CBOs/NGOs/Collaborators<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cbos-ngos-collaborators" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>These are organisations which look after the interests of the visually impaired. They provide assistance in the form of materials and equipment, education, finances, and provision of guidance for the visually impaired.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="sight-savers-international">Sight Savers International<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sight-savers-international" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The headquarters of this organisation is in England. The organisation provides resources and materials to help the visually impaired.</p>
<p>This organisation channels the grants through regional offices in Nairobi to the beneficiaries. The sight savers international is the sponsor of the integrated programmes through the Kenya Society for the blind.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="salvation-army">Salvation Army<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#salvation-army" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This organisation collaborates with Thika school for the blind.</p>
<p>Thika school for the blind offers primary and secondary school education for the blind.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="low-vision-project">Low Vision Project<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#low-vision-project" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This project is based in Kikuyu pentecostal church of east africa hospital, and it provides services to people with low vision.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="other-organisations">Other Organisations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#other-organisations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Christofell Blinden Mission (C.B.M)</li>
<li>Sallus Ocullic</li>
<li>Catholic church</li>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management-and-prevention-of-visual-impairment">Management and Prevention of Visual Impairment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-and-prevention-of-visual-impairment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The management of persons with visual impairment starts with the proper assessment of the condition followed by treatment, integration and rehabilitation.</p>
<p>Assessment can be done either in a hospital or through mobile outreach units including school visits by health workers. Once the problem has been properly diagnosed, then the treatment may include surgery or visual aids, such as the fitting of eye glasses.</p>
<p>If after assessment a person is found to be completely visually impaired, they will need to be integrated and rehabilitated into the community.</p>
<p>The process of integration and rehabilitation once again starts at the family level, and continues into the community through special schools and other institutions for the visually impaired.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 187 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="prevention-of-visual-impairment">Prevention of Visual Impairment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-visual-impairment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>There are a number of measures you can take to prevent visual impairment in your communities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prenatal-stage">Prenatal Stage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prenatal-stage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Advise pregnant mothers to avoid taking any medicines unless prescribed by the doctor.</li>
<li>Educate pregnant mothers on the need for proper prenatal care in order to prevent infections, early diagnosis and management of conditions if they occur and their complications.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="administration">Administration<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#administration" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Administration of the following measures:</p>
<ul>
<li>All primary immunisations should be completed</li>
<li>Application of tetracycline eye ointments to newborns at birth</li>
<li>Giving vitamin A capsules to children suffering from measles</li>
<li>Control of diabetes and the blood pressure</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nutrition">Nutrition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nutrition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The diet should be rich in Vitamin A and B to avoid changes in the retina, conjunctiva and cornea.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="wearing-protective-devices">Wearing Protective Devices<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#wearing-protective-devices" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In activities that pose a danger of injury to the eye from foreign objectives, for example, hairsprays, ultraviolet rays and bright sun.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lighting">Lighting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lighting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Adequate and well placed lighting in the rooms to avoid straining of the eyes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="personal-hygiene">Personal Hygiene<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#personal-hygiene" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Educating members of the community of the importance of good personal hygiene, for example, a daily bath, keeping eyes clean especially when they are infected, in order to avoid attracting flies.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="early-diagnosis-and-treatment">Early Diagnosis and Treatment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#early-diagnosis-and-treatment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Prompt and correct treatment of all common eye infections and especially trachoma.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="care-of-children-in-need">Care of Children in Need<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#care-of-children-in-need" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A child in need is one who has been abandoned, orphaned, or one whose parents are incapable of looking after them properly. Such a child needs the best possible alternative arrangements for their care in the absence of the parents.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="needs-of-the-children">Needs of the Children<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#needs-of-the-children" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Nutritional needs. Most of these children are malnourished.</li>
<li>Parental love.</li>
<li>Lack of education.</li>
<li>Lack of access to health care. such as AIDS orphans who are themselves infected.</li>
<li>Security and protection from harmful practices like female genital mutilation, child labour, forced marriage.</li>
<li>Stigma and discrimination such as those orphaned by AIDS.</li>
<li>Social burden such as care for the other children or for a terminally ill parent.</li>
<li>Poverty due to lack of a source of income to care for themselves and the family.</li>
<li>Inadequate or lack of shelter.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-kinds-of-services-are-available-for-children-in-need-in-your-community">What kinds of services are available for children in need in your community?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-kinds-of-services-are-available-for-children-in-need-in-your-community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="children-s-homes">Children's Homes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#children-s-homes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>These homes are owned and run by individuals with the help of donors and well wishers. They provide the children with their basic needs and education. These homes are supervised by the department of children under the ministry of social services.</p>
<p>Approved schools, for example Kirigiti in Kiambu, Wamumu in Mwea and many others. These are run by the government.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="remand-homes">Remand Homes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remand-homes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>These are available in your communities and they are run by social services.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 188 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hospitals">Hospitals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hospitals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Most of the abandoned children are brought to the hospitals. Here they are cared for and then handed over to the children's department for adoption, or are later taken to homes or institutions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="integration-and-rehabilitation">Integration and Rehabilitation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#integration-and-rehabilitation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>When these children grow and attend school or acquire some skills they are able to be independent by getting employment or by becoming self-employed. In this way they become useful members of the community.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="reduction-of-children-in-need">Reduction of Children in Need<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reduction-of-children-in-need" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>You can reduce the number of children in need by:</p>
<ul>
<li>Strengthening family relationships in the community, so that such children are taken care of by their immediate family members, especially orphans. This will provide a conducive environment for the child to grow in.</li>
<li>Providing family life education to the youth on consequences of pre-marital sex, as many of the abandoned children are as a result of unwanted pregnancies.</li>
<li>Implementing safe motherhood initiatives in order to prevent maternal deaths.</li>
<li>Providing family planning services, so that families get the number of children they can manage.</li>
<li>Providing information to the community members on the services available for adoption. This would help those members in the community who have no children of their own, as well as those with unwanted pregnancies</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="care-of-the-elderly">Care of the Elderly<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#care-of-the-elderly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The ageing process is often defined in terms of physical changes that negatively affect the body's function and appearance. Old age is associated with poor health, poverty and dependency.</p>
<p>In the past, our traditional support systems were so effective that they made the problems of the elderly insignificant. However, today these support systems have disintegrated due to socio-economic changes in our society.</p>
<p>In Kenya, the elderly are defined as persons aged 64 years and above, although the retirement age is 55 years of age. In this subsection you will consider an elderly person as anyone who has attained the age of 60 years and above.</p>
<p>The number of elderly citizens in this country has been on the increase. This increase would not be of much concern if you already had support structures in place to take care of them. However, as mentioned earlier, these systems have disintegrated leaving them vulnerable to medical and social problems.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="problems-of-the-elderly">Problems of the Elderly<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#problems-of-the-elderly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-five-problems-of-the-elderly">List five problems of the elderly.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-five-problems-of-the-elderly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following are problems of the elderly:</p>
<ul>
<li>Poverty</li>
<li>Loneliness</li>
<li>Poor nutrition</li>
<li>Physical handicap</li>
<li>Dental problem</li>
<li>Mental problems</li>
<li>Lack of energy to provide activities of daily living</li>
<li>Inadequate housing</li>
<li>Chronic illnesses</li>
<li>Age related changes such as immobility and presbyopia</li>
<li>Lack of care in sickness</li>
</ul>
<p>These problems are experienced by the elderly throughout the world, although they may vary in some cases, depending on the kind of support available in the community.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="available-services-for-the-elderly">Available Services for the Elderly<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#available-services-for-the-elderly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="at-the-family-level">At the Family Level<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#at-the-family-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In Kenya most elderly people live with their nucleus and extended family. These are the people who care for them.</p>
<p>As a community health nurse, it is your responsibility to encourage families to care for their elderly persons. You need to educate them on the needs of the elderly, equip them with the necessary knowledge, skills and attitudes to provide effective care.</p>
<p>You also need to educate members of the community on the importance of planning for retirement. The aim for this preparation is to help the elderly persons remain independent and comfortable in their own homes as long as</p>
<p>possible. There is need to discuss the payment of pensions and allowances early for better planning.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="at-the-community-level">At the Community Level<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#at-the-community-level" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Elderly persons require community health services. It is your responsibility to identify them and make sure they are available and accessible to the elderly persons. Encourage them to join recreation facilities to improve their mobility and to join peer groups to help them psychologically.</p>
<p>During home visiting you should be able to provide direct care to the elderly. Churches also provide spiritual support as well as material support to the elderly persons. The women and youth groups offer different types of care. When these groups visit the elderly they alleviate their loneliness and improve their nutrition status by providing them with meals. They also help them with cleaning, repair work and gardening.</p>
<p>As a health worker, one of your important roles is to become their advocates. You should let their needs be known by the community and motivate them, especially the youth, to have a positive attitude towards care of the elderly, so that you add life into their days.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="institutions-for-the-elderly">Institutions for the Elderly<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#institutions-for-the-elderly" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In Kenya, there are a number of homes for the elderly and day care centres.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="do-you-have-any-in-your-district">Do you have any in your district?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#do-you-have-any-in-your-district" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If you do not know, then you need to identify these homes.</p>
<p>They provide the following services:</p>
<ul>
<li>Nutrition</li>
<li>Activities of daily living such as personal hygiene</li>
<li>Treatment of any sickness</li>
<li>Recreational activities</li>
<li>Safety and comfort</li>
</ul>
<p>The best care for the elderly is the one provided by the family.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hospitals">Hospitals<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hospitals" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Geriatric hospitals are well established in developed countries.</p>
<p>In Kenya the elderly do not have any special health services targeting them. In some communities it is commonly believed that old age is a cause of illness. This leads to delay in seeking health care for the elderly.</p>
<p>Another reason why the elderly may delay to seek health care, is that they live far from the health services. As a community health nurse, it is your responsibility to sensitise and encourage community members to seek health care for their elderly persons.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-chronically-ill">The Chronically Ill<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-chronically-ill" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-is-chronic-illness">What is chronic illness?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-is-chronic-illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An illness is said to be chronic if it meets one or more of the following criteria:</p>
<ul>
<li>Permanent</li>
<li>Leaves a residual disability</li>
<li>Caused by non-reversible pathological conditions</li>
<li>Requires special rehabilitative training of the patient</li>
<li>Requires long term supervision and care</li>
</ul>
<p>Examples of chronic illnesses include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Diabetes mellitus</li>
<li>Arthritis</li>
<li>Hypertension</li>
<li>Sickle cell disease</li>
<li>Renal disease</li>
<li>Heart disease</li>
<li>Terminal carcinoma and other debilitating diseases</li>
<li>AIDS</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="imposes-limits">Imposes Limits<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#imposes-limits" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The idea of limits is sometimes expressed metaphorically, as living within an energy envelope, having an energy bank account with a very low balance, or seeing available energy as a bowl of marbles, which must be spent very carefully.</p>
<p>Living well with chronic illness means learning to live within limits and learning to manage powerful emotions.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="affects-many-parts-of-life">Affects Many Parts of Life<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#affects-many-parts-of-life" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Chronic illness affects many parts of life, such as, the ability to work, relationships, emotions, dreams for the future and personal integrity.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 189 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 190 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="brings-uncertainty">Brings Uncertainty<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#brings-uncertainty" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Chronic illness brings great uncertainty, both on a
day to day basis, as symptoms wax and wane, and over longer cycles.</p>
<p>They may be concerned about their finances, worrying about whether they will be able to support themselves, or whether they can qualify for or keep up with the disability.</p>
<p>When they think about the future, they may worry about how far down they may slide, and about becoming dependent or financially destitute. They may feel at times that they have lost control over their bodies, and over their ability to plan and predict.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="varies-greatly-in-severity">Varies Greatly in Severity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#varies-greatly-in-severity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Just as chronic illness is comprehensive in its effects, so too is it tremendously varied. Some people have relatively mild cases, while others may be bedridden. Most people are somewhere in between.</p>
<p>There are many different patterns of symptoms. The bottom line is that each person's illness is different.</p>
<p>Adding to the complexity, an individual's illness may vary over time. Some symptoms may disappear, only to be replaced by new ones. Some people may have a relatively stable course, while others may fluctuate between times of severe symptoms and times of remission.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="varies-depending-on-life-situation">Varies Depending on Life Situation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#varies-depending-on-life-situation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The financial situations of patients vary enormously.</p>
<p>Some continue to work, have spouses who work, or receive generous disability payments. They may find their financial situation to be similar to what it was before becoming ill.</p>
<p>For others, however, financial pressures can be overwhelming. Some patients have little or no income.</p>
<p>Qualifying for disability can be a long and stressful ordeal. Those with disability may worry about losing it. Others feel forced to work even when their bodies cry out asking for rest.</p>
<p>The quality of relationships may vary greatly too. Some patients receive good support from family and friends.</p>
<p>For others, relationships are a source of great stress. For all, however, chronic illness changes
relationships, creating new strains and frustrations.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="will-be-affected-by-one-s-response">Will be Affected by One's Response<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#will-be-affected-by-one-s-response" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Chronic illness calls for a different role for patients and doctors than is typically true for short-term illness.</p>
<p>The doctor has limited powers, because there are no cures for chronic conditions and medications often have limited effectiveness.</p>
<p>In chronic illness, much more responsibility falls on the shoulders of patients, the people who manage their illness on a day to day basis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="available-services-for-the-chronically-ill">Available Services for the Chronically Ill<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#available-services-for-the-chronically-ill" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A chronic condition does not only affect the patient, but also all the family members who live with the affected person.</p>
<p>This is because most chronic diseases bring about dependency and an extra financial burden on the family. A number of services are available for the chronically ill at the family, community and institutional levels.</p>
