<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="family">Family<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#family" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Often, chronically ill patients are taken care of at home by family members. This is known as home-based care which you will learn more about it in the next unit of this module. In order for a family to care properly for a chronically ill patient, they need to be prepared and educated on the requirements.</p>
<p>It is your responsibility to provide them with the necessary information and to follow up on the patient's progress from time to time. This is important as it helps the family and the patient to feel confident in the care at home.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="community">Community<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Community Health Workers (CHW), as well as Community Owned Resource Persons (CORPS), can assist the family to care for a chronically ill person at home. This can take the form of medical advice, material support and spiritual support.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="available-services-for-the-critically-ill">Available Services for the Critically Ill<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#available-services-for-the-critically-ill" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="institutions">Institutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#institutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Institutions that provide services to the chronically ill include hospitals, hospices, and</p>
<p>support groups depending on the type of chronic illness.</p>
<p>Hospitals admit these patients during the acute stage for management. Once this stage is over, they are then discharged and followed up at the consultant clinics, from where they are given medication to take at home.</p>
<p>Hospices usually take care of terminally ill patients. They teach the patients and their caregivers all issues concerning care, and also make follow up visits at home, where the patients are being cared for.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-chronically-ill-patients">Management of Chronically Ill Patients<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-chronically-ill-patients" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The management of chronically ill patients depends on the stage of adaptation to the illness that the patient is in.</p>
<p>In the first stage, they tend to be in denial and disbelief. During this stage you need to be actively involved in the care of this patient even if they are being cared for at home. Educate the family members to listen to all the expressions of feeling by the patient without criticising them. They should also be empathetic and listen to the arguments without being judgmental.</p>
<p>Patients in the second stage of adaptation to their illness commonly manifest with anger. During this stage the patient develops an awareness of the chronic illness. You should educate the caregivers to exercise restraint and self control.</p>
<p>In the third stage the patient undergoes reorganisation and is nourished by the concept of hope. You should therefore give hope generously within acceptable limits. You should also provide the patient and family with suitable and practical coping methods, and encourage the use of self-help devices if necessary.</p>
<p>Knowing the patient's values, religion and beliefs will go along way in assisting you help the patient.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention-of-chronic-illnesses">Prevention of Chronic Illnesses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention-of-chronic-illnesses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="primary-prevention">Primary Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Provision of good prenatal, intrapartum and delivery care.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Genetic counselling is done in cases where there is a genetic risk, for example, in diabetes mellitus and sickle cell disease.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Discouraging risky habits, such as smoking and over consumption of alcohol, in order to reduce chances of lung conditions, liver cirrhosis and mental disorders.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Early diagnosis and treatment of these conditions.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Regular exercises.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A healthy diet low in calories and animal fat, to prevent obesity, heart and blood vessel diseases.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="secondary-prevention">Secondary Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secondary-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Regular medical checkups.</li>
<li>Screening measures, such as, pap smear, self breast examination. Screening should take place at home, school and community levels.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="tertiary-prevention">Tertiary Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tertiary-prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Tertiary prevention includes, first aid, treatment and rehabilitation of diseases. It aims at preventing complications and disability.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="displaced-persons">Displaced Persons<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#displaced-persons" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are people who have been displaced from their communities or even countries.</p>
<p>The displacement of people can be caused by a number of factors, the most common being armed conflict. Natural disasters, famine, political reasons and economic changes are some of the others.</p>
<p>They can be divided into two categories:</p>
<ul>
<li>Internally displaced persons</li>
<li>Externally displaced persons</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="internally-displaced-persons">Internally Displaced Persons<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#internally-displaced-persons" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>These are people who have been displaced within their country, following ethnic clashes or disasters such as floods and earthquakes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="externally-displaced-persons">Externally Displaced Persons<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#externally-displaced-persons" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>These are people who have run away from their country as a result of civil war or political persecution.</p>
<p>They are also known as refugees. For example in Kenya there are many refugees from neighbouring countries such as Sudan and Somalia.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>The government works closely with the United Nations High Commission for Refugees (UNHCR) to settle all externally displaced persons.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="list-down-four-problems-encountered-by-displaced-persons">List down four problems encountered by displaced persons.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#list-down-four-problems-encountered-by-displaced-persons" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The problems experienced by displaced persons include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Housing</li>
<li>Sanitation</li>
<li>Water supply</li>
<li>Lack of inadequate nutrition which may result in malnutrition</li>
<li>Security risk and human rights violation</li>
<li>Overcrowding which may cause rapid spread of diseases</li>
<li>Lack of education opportunities</li>
<li>Lack of health services</li>
<li>Emotional needs</li>
<li>Poverty</li>
</ul>
<p>Displaced persons tend to develop health problems due to poor living conditions, as well as psychological and physical trauma caused by displacement.</p>
<p>Some displaced persons are separated from their families and relatives and have lost homes, jobs and schools for their children. They need material as well as psychological care. Some may develop antisocial behaviour as a defence mechanism, as they are unhappy with the displacement. It is important that some measures be taken to help them.</p>
<p>Apart from the above problems, people who have been displaced may bring new diseases, such as diarrhoeal diseases, typhoid, measles, meningitis, sexually transmitted diseases, and HIV/AIDS.</p>
<p>Even their animals can bring in diseases such as rabies, anthrax, foot and mouth and brucellosis. So as you can see, they can also pose as a health risk to the community where they settle.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="effects-of-displacement-of-people">Effects of Displacement of People<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-displacement-of-people" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Displacement often leads to dramatic changes in the family structure and gender roles, relations and identities.</p>
<p>In conflict situations, many women are suddenly thrust into the role of head of the household because the men are recruited to combat, they stay behind to maintain land, or migrate in search of work.</p>
<p>There is also:</p>
<ul>
<li>Escalation in the level of poverty</li>
<li>Reduction in the level of foreign aid</li>
<li>Demographic consequences</li>
<li>Religious effect</li>
<li>Conflicts between the host community and the displaced group</li>
<li>Political effect</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="services-available">Services Available<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#services-available" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The services available for displaced persons tend to be those provided by relief agencies, NGOs, the government through the provincial and district administration, the church, and institutions such as UNCHR which take care of external refugees.</p>
<p>They provide them with shelter, medical care, food and clothing, and sometimes rehabilitation in the form of teaching them new skills.</p>
<p>Refugees have some sort of international protection. Their needs are catered for by UNHCR and their rights are also protected.</p>
<p>Internally displaced people are still citizens of their country, and are not afforded protection.</p>
<p>The International Committee of the Red Cross (ICRC) protects the rights of internally displaced people. It conducts protection and assistance programmes for these victims.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="management-of-displaced-persons">Management of Displaced Persons<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management-of-displaced-persons" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Your role as a community health nurse, will be to work with other health workers as a team, in order to deal with the various problems of displaced people.</p>
<p>There will be a need to set up relief centres which provide the following services:</p>
<ul>
<li>Screening and first aid to all new arrivals.</li>
<li>Food assistance, especially to infants and children, as food is a basic need. The adults also need food for survival.</li>
<li>Temporary shelter so that individuals can sleep and rest.</li>
<li>Reproductive health services; antenatal, labour, delivery and post natal, family planning services are also provided.</li>
<li>Medical care services, where curative care for common diseases and injuries will be provided.</li>
<li>Immunisation programmes for children and pregnant mothers.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 192 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Health education and community mobilisation.</li>
<li>Identification and the use of the community health workers in the area is necessary.</li>
</ul>
<p>As these emergency services are given, the families should be encouraged to settle down, especially if the situation requires them to stay there for a long period. They should be encouraged to start growing their own food and rearing their own animals.</p>
<p>Having looked at the special health services needed by displaced persons, Next you will consider the needs of another group, that is, widows and widowers. Do they require any care and what can you do for them?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="widows-widowers">Widows/Widowers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#widows-widowers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The death of a spouse makes one to become a widow or widower and you have many of them in your community. Some of the leading causes of death today in Kenya include diseases and road traffic accidents.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="think-of-four-diseases-that-are-a-major-cause-of-mortality-in-kenya">Think of four diseases that are a major cause of mortality in Kenya.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#think-of-four-diseases-that-are-a-major-cause-of-mortality-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The following diseases are a major cause of morbidity and mortality in Kenya:</p>
<ul>
<li>HIV/AIDS.</li>
<li>Malaria.</li>
<li>Hypertension.</li>
<li>Typhoid.</li>
<li>Diabetes mellitus.</li>
<li>Heart diseases.</li>
<li>Diarrhoeal diseases.</li>
<li>Obstetric complications, such as pregnancy induced hypertension, ante partum haemorrhage and postpartum haemorrhage.</li>
</ul>
<p>As mentioned earlier, apart from disease, the second most common cause of death in Kenya is road traffic accidents.</p>
<p>The factors that contribute to road traffic accidents include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Unroadworthy vehicles.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Careless driving, usually under the influence of substance abuse.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Poor enforcement of traffic regulations by the concerned authorities.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Unskilled drivers.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Poor roads.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>When a spouse dies the effect of the loss affects the entire family. They not only lose the love and care from that parent or spouse, but sometimes also the financial support. Therefore widows/widowers require a lot of support, empathy, understanding, love and care. They need to surround themselves with people who they can trust and rely on.</p>
<p>This tends to be people who have been close, understanding and supportive to the family. They are people whom the family has shared important aspects of their life with, and are referred to as significant others. They include members of the extended family, friends, colleagues, church members, and so on. They help the family to cope with feelings of loss.</p>
<p>As a community health nurse, your role is mainly to counsel the widow or widower, and to support them as they go through the grieving process.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="needs-of-widows">Needs of Widows<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#needs-of-widows" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Psychological effects following the death of the husband, such as loneliness, and cultural practices not allowing the widow to re-marry.</li>
<li>Poverty, due to not having the right to inherit property or have their right enforced, being evicted from their property, no support from family or relatives.</li>
<li>Basic needs such as food and shelter can not be met due to poverty, resulting from unemployment and illiteracy.</li>
<li>Support to care for the left children. Children especially girls are in an extremely vulnerable position, due to early marriage and child labour.</li>
<li>Vulnerable to violence, sexual abuse and rape.</li>
<li>Exploitation at work place due to homelessness, illiteracy and poverty.</li>
<li>Love and belonging. Some may be rejected by the family.</li>
<li>Health needs for the whole family or the left spouse. This is especially so if she was sick, as in the case of AIDS or if both were involved in an accident, which killed one and left the other injured.</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 193 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Marriage, especially where men are culturally supposed to marry when their spouses die.</li>
<li>Intense loneliness due to lack of previously established relationship. This may result in hurried replacement of the wife.</li>
<li>Severely affected health and well-being because widowers are not able to care for themselves since most of the care was provided by the wife.</li>
<li>Immense feelings which may result in physical and psychological symptoms such as sexual fear due to loss of a loved one, social isolation.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="services-available-for-widows-and-widowers">Services Available for Widows and Widowers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#services-available-for-widows-and-widowers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In developed countries there are well established systems in place for helping widows or widowers.</p>
<p>However in Kenya there are no formal systems, although within many communities there are various support systems which can be mobilised to assist a widow or widower.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-extended-family-members">The Extended Family Members<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-extended-family-members" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In many communities, the traditional support system for a widow or widower is the extended family. They support the widow during the grieving period and sometimes take the responsibility of caring for the family. They also identify ways of assisting the widow or widower and in many cases conduct fund raisings or 'harambees' to help them meet expenses such as hospital bills or school fees for the children. This is a spirit which you need to cherish.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="clan">Clan<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clan" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In certain communities, clans play a very big role in the care of a widow. The clan takes the responsibilities of the children's education, and may even assign individual members of the family, the responsibility over the children, in order to ensure that the burden is well shared out.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="support-groups">Support Groups<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#support-groups" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Support groups for widows and widowers are common and exist in most of our communities. They come together to share their problems and help each other in solving them.</p>
<p>They also contribute money, and sometimes look for donors to help them establish income-generating activities. A good example is the group known as Widows and Orphans of AIDS Kenya (WOFAK).</p>
<p>As a community health nurse you should find out about these groups, so that you can advice and encourage widows and widowers to join them for support.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="institutions">Institutions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#institutions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As mentioned earlier, in Kenya there are no established institutions designed to take care of widow and widowers. However, the government has established a system known as the widow and widowers pension scheme.</p>
<p>This scheme pays a pension to the widow or widower as well as allowances for the children. It is important to remember that the widow and widower pension scheme only covers those who are employed by the government. For the unemployed the family and community takes the responsibility.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 194 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 195 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="section-2-disaster-management">SECTION 2: DISASTER MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#section-2-disaster-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Welcome to the second section of the unit on special health issues. In this section you shall cover disaster management, its elements, as well as disaster prevention, mitigation, response, recovery and development.</p>
<p>In all forms of injury or disease it is possible to apply first aid measures before the actual diagnosis and treatment can be applied. Such measures aim at reducing complications or preventing the injury from becoming worse. The measures may be performed by the victims themselves or by other people who are around the victim. If the measures are conducted in a professional manner then the victim is assured of a good prognosis. The same rationale applies to disaster management.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>By the end of this unit you will be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Define disaster</li>
<li>Describe the causes and effect of disaster in the community</li>
<li>Explain the Kenya national plan for disaster management</li>
<li>Describe how to prepare the community for disaster management</li>
<li>Describe the concept of triaging in disaster management</li>
<li>Describe the health care activities during disaster recovery</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="overview-of-disasters">Overview of Disasters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#overview-of-disasters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Kenya has had its share of disasters. You will have heard of fires in boarding schools, hotels and slum areas; natural disasters such as droughts, landslides and floods; and disease outbreaks such as cholera, yellow fever and currently HIV/AIDS. All these are different forms of disasters.</p>
<p>Like many other developing countries, Kenya only deals with disasters after they have occurred. Although the people are always ready to act in emergencies and have in the past put up valiant rescue efforts, there is a great need for the government to train different personnel on disaster preparedness and management. The experience of the 1998 bomb blast in Nairobi was a good indicator. Indeed, all communities need to be prepared to be ready for such eventualities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-would-you-define-the-term-disaster">How would you define the term "disaster"?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-would-you-define-the-term-disaster" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A disaster is a catastrophic phenomenon or series of phenomena natural or man-made, that threaten(s) or cause(s) widespread severe injury or loss of life or property or both on a scale sufficient to warrant extraordinary response from outside the community. It can also be defined as a sudden, accidental event that causes many deaths and injuries. Most disasters also result in significant property damage.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-are-the-common-causes-of-disasters">What are the Common Causes of Disasters?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-common-causes-of-disasters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Today, forces of nature such as earthquakes, accidents, or even terrorist activities can cause disasters.</p>
<p>The natural causes of disasters include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Earthquakes</li>
<li>Floods</li>
<li>Hurricanes</li>
<li>Typhoons</li>
<li>Tornadoes</li>
<li>Tsunamis (popularly, but incorrectly, known as tidal waves)</li>
<li>Volcanic eruptions</li>
<li>Wildfires</li>
<li>Landslides and</li>
<li>Avalanches</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-are-the-common-causes-of-disasters">What are the Common Causes of Disasters?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-are-the-common-causes-of-disasters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Disasters, which are caused by accidents, include those due to plane crashes, sinking ferries, collapsing buildings, bridges or mines as well as explosions and fires accidentally triggered by man.</p>
<p>Thus disasters can be classified into two, namely:</p>
<ul>
<li>Natural disasters</li>
<li>Man-made disasters</li>
</ul>
<p>Each type of disaster has its own special features. Some disasters can be foreseen several hours, days, months or even years beforehand, for example, hurricanes, cyclones and earthquakes. Others such as a plane crash or road traffic accident occur without the slightest warning.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="effects-of-disasters">Effects of Disasters<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#effects-of-disasters" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The most obvious effects of disasters are physical and psychological trauma, sickness and death. These depend on the type of disaster, whether it is an earthquake, fire, drought, floods or a disease outbreak and its severity.</p>
<p>Earthquakes have a high level of mortality as victims tend to be crushed by falling objects. The risk of injury is greatest inside or near dwellings but is very small in the open field. Also, earthquakes, which take place at night are more deadly with larger numbers of injuries such as fractures to the pelvis, thorax and spine. This is because most people are caught sleeping and are oblivious of what is going on. Earthquakes that take place during the day tend to cause injuries of the limbs, collarbone and skull as the victims attempt to flee from collapsing buildings.</p>
<p>Disasters which involve fire, such as explosions or electrical malfunctions tend to cause varying degrees of burns in the victims. The victims may also suffer from suffocation due to smoke inhalation or air pollution as in the case of volcanic eruptions.</p>
<p>For example, in 1985 23,000 people died in Colombia following volcanic eruptions which were accompanied by mudslides and glowing clouds.</p>
<p>More recently you have heard of the "tsunami" tidal wave which killed thousands of people in Indonesia and left many others homeless. The survivors were suffering from varying degrees of bruising, fractures and hypothermia. Although cyclones and hurricanes do not cause high mortality rates like tidal waves, they cause houses to collapse and carry objects in the wind which can cause injuries like fractures, cuts and bruises on the victims they strike.</p>
<p>Drought causes famine that leads to malnutrition, for example, protein calorie malnutrition, kwashiorkor, marasmus and vitamin A deficiency or xerophthalmia.</p>
<p>War can result into either internal or external displacement of people.</p>
<p>You shall now look at the situation analysis for Kenya, that is, the recent history of disasters in the country, the hazard profile and government policy on disaster management.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="situation-analysis-for-kenya">Situation Analysis for Kenya<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#situation-analysis-for-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Disasters that have hit Kenya in the last 30 years have been caused by different types of hazards, such as, droughts, fires, flooding, bomb blast and accidents in the transport industry. Dealing with some of these disasters has at times required major national and international response and recovery operations.</p>
<p>Recent History of Disasters in Kenya</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Year</th><th>Types of Disaster</th><th>Area of Coverage</th><th>No of People Affected</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1999/2000</td><td>Drought</td><td>Widespread</td><td>4.4 million</td></tr><tr><td>August 1998</td><td>Terrorism</td><td>Nairobi</td><td>214 killed and 5,600 injured</td></tr><tr><td>1997/1998</td><td>El Nino Flood</td><td>Widespread</td><td>1.5 million</td></tr><tr><td>1995/1996</td><td>Drought</td><td>Widespread</td><td>1.4 million</td></tr><tr><td>1994</td><td>Ferry accident</td><td>Mtongwe channel</td><td>270 died</td></tr><tr><td>1992</td><td>Train Accident</td><td>Mtilo Andei</td><td>31 died, 207 were injured</td></tr><tr><td>1991/ 92</td><td>Drought</td><td>Arid and Semi Arid Districts of NE, Rift, Eastern and Coast Provinces</td><td>1.5 million</td></tr><tr><td>1990</td><td>Fire</td><td>Lamu</td><td>20 died</td></tr><tr><td>1985</td><td>Floods</td><td>Nyanza/Western</td><td>10,000</td></tr><tr><td>1984/2001</td><td>HIV/AIDS</td><td>Widespread and continuing</td><td>2.2 million dead by 2001</td></tr><tr><td>1983/84</td><td>Drought</td><td>Widespread</td><td>200,000</td></tr><tr><td>1982</td><td>Fire</td><td>Nairobi</td><td>10,000</td></tr><tr><td>1982</td><td>Floods</td><td>Nyanza</td><td>4,000</td></tr><tr><td>1982</td><td>Fire</td><td>Lamu</td><td>4,000</td></tr><tr><td>1980</td><td>Drought</td><td>Widespread</td><td>40,000</td></tr><tr><td>1977</td><td>Drought</td><td>Widespread</td><td>20,000</td></tr><tr><td>1975</td><td>Drought</td><td>Widespread</td><td>16,000</td></tr><tr><td>1971</td><td>Drought</td><td>Widespread</td><td>150,000</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="hazard-profile">Hazard Profile<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hazard-profile" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The Kenyan government has identified the principal hazards that need to be addressed in the country.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 196 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>HIV/AIDS and disease epidemics</li>
<li>Livestock and wildlife diseases</li>
<li>Transport accidents</li>
<li>Lightening</li>
<li>Pest invasion</li>
<li>Drug, alcohol and substance abuse</li>
<li>Fires</li>
</ul>
<p>These are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Drought</li>
<li>Floods</li>
<li>Landslides</li>
<li>Earthquakes and volcanic activity</li>
<li>Terrorism</li>
<li>Civil conflict</li>
<li>Industrial hazards and pollution</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-do-disasters-affect-the-development-of-an-area">How do Disasters Affect the Development of an Area?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-do-disasters-affect-the-development-of-an-area" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Disasters throw everybody and everything in disarray both at individual, family or community levels. There is loss of life, property and infrastructure. All these cause delay and retardation of development in the area. However life must go on, and so people need to be mobilised to rescue, recover, readjust and reconstruct. In some instances people must start from zero.</p>
<p>There are many lessons which can be learned after a disaster, which if properly used may reduce the impact of damage should the disaster strike again, or prevent the disaster altogether.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lessons-learned-from-disasters-in-kenya">Lessons Learned from Disasters in Kenya<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lessons-learned-from-disasters-in-kenya" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Following disasters which have taken place in Kenya several committees have met and discussed information gathered and lessons learned.</p>
<p>They have come up with the following recommendations:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>That disaster management must include all key actors in a multi-agency and intersectoral approach.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There is need for effective early warning and quick dissemination of information to all actors. A combined effort helps to utilise resources and is more cost effective.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The disaster management system needs long term funding. This is a state of preparedness for any eventuality.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The disaster management system needs flexible budgeting and rapid financial disbursement procedures. You need to harness the good will of communities to be responsive to your call when in need.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The system must facilitate community participation. In the absence of finances the community might be in a position to provide aid in other forms. It is good to have this on record so that they can be called upon when need arises.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The system must be able to collect, document and disseminate information and undertake research.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The system must emphasise public education and awareness on disaster management.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>That the government should set aside funds to cater for disaster management.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>That a policy should be formulated to specifically address disaster issues in consultation with experts from within and without.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="kenya-national-policy-on-disaster-management">Kenya National Policy on Disaster Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#kenya-national-policy-on-disaster-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In view of the experiences gained and lessons learned during management of various disasters, the government has committed itself and formulated a policy that emphasises proactive and preventive strategies in addressing disaster situations.</p>
<p>The policy outlines the need to reduce exposure of vulnerable communities to risk and promote a sustainable disaster management system. The policy also outlines the goals, objectives and guidelines for disaster management.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="goal">Goal<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#goal" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>To establish and maintain an efficient, flexible and coordinated system for managing disasters, in order to minimise losses and resulting disruptions on the population, economy and environment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="objectives">Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The specific objectives to be met by Kenya are as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>To establish an institutional framework that will manage disasters</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 197 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>To ensure that institutions involved in disaster management are well coordinated and focused on both risks and vulnerability reduction</li>
<li>To promote the linkages between disaster management and development planning</li>
<li>To foster partnerships, between the government and stakeholders at all levels, including regional and international bodies</li>
<li>To promote programmes and strategies that reduce the vulnerability of Kenyans to hazards</li>
<li>To provide adequate and specific funds for disaster management</li>
<li>To mobilise adequate resources to ensure effective implementation of the policy, subsequent strategies and programmes.</li>
<li>To promote disaster management culture, training, research, information dissemination, community awareness and preparedness.</li>
</ul>
<p>Although these are broad objectives for the entire country, they can guide you to plan disaster management strategies at the community level. Various countries today have set up systems for protecting the civilian population in the event of disasters. Since the August 7th 1998 bomb blast, Kenya has also embarked on organising such preparations. A National Disaster Management Authority (NADIMA) has been proposed.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20260117-3145be5f.jpeg" alt="img-1.jpeg">
Organisational Structure of the Proposed NADIMA</p>
<p>The government has also come up with policy elements which form the basis of the country's disaster management policy. You will now briefly look at the policy elements.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-policy-elements">The Policy Elements<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-policy-elements" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are four policy elements which underpin Kenya's disaster management policy. These are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Prevention</li>
<li>Mitigation</li>
<li>Preparedness</li>
<li>Response and recovery</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="prevention">Prevention<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#prevention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This element focuses on measures aimed at preventing the occurrence of a disaster and minimising its harmful effects on the community, property and the environment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mitigation">Mitigation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mitigation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Mitigation is increasing the population's ability to cope with disaster most likely to affect them.</p>
<p>Why do you think it is important to increase a community's ability to respond to disaster?</p>
<p>This is because in a well organised community, it is easier for you to improve the quality of</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>outside assistance and reduce the shortcomings that often occur during disaster.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="what-do-you-think-are-some-of-these-shortcomings">What do you think are some of these shortcomings?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#what-do-you-think-are-some-of-these-shortcomings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Lack of background information</li>
<li>Poor educational requirements</li>
<li>Provision of inappropriate type of aid</li>
</ul>
<p>Information systems, risk information, vulnerability analysis, early warning system, advocacy and public awareness, training, resource inventory, public safety and research and development are issues that must be singly addressed under mitigation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="information-systems">Information Systems<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#information-systems" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The National Disaster Management Authority should generate and collate early warning information from relevant ministries and other sources. This information should be disseminated to users in the government's disaster management network and external networks, right down to the communities.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="risk-information">Risk Information<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#risk-information" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A disaster management system should be established at all levels to coordinate the collection, collation, analysis and dissemination of risk information.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vulnerability-analysis">Vulnerability Analysis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vulnerability-analysis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This links directly to mitigation activities and provides the context of understanding the effect of any hazard on the population, property and the environment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="early-warning-system">Early Warning System<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#early-warning-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Provides early warning information on impending disasters and helps to plan for preparedness and response activities. The policy encourages involvement of all stakeholders with regards to information provision, analysis and decision-making.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="advocacy-and-public-awareness">Advocacy and Public Awareness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#advocacy-and-public-awareness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This should be undertaken to sensitise the population on the policy and increase people's understanding of the disasters they are likely to face. The policy supports the development of community based disaster initiatives.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="training">Training<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#training" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>For effective disaster management and sustainability of programmes capacity building and training in disaster management will be emphasised. The training includes all people of a community making use of their respective areas of specialisation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="resource-inventory">Resource Inventory<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#resource-inventory" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In order to increase the capacity to respond quickly to disasters, a comprehensive and all inclusive resource inventory will be established. The government is prepared to fund research whose findings will be disseminated to users for decision-making and utilised in the development planning process.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="public-safety">Public Safety<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#public-safety" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The promotion of public safety must be given priority.</p>
<p>The government will ensure adherence to professional and safety standards and ethics.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="research-and-development">Research and Development<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#research-and-development" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Research will be funded and findings will be disseminated to users for decision making and utilised in development and planning process.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparedness-and-response">Preparedness and Response<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparedness-and-response" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p><strong>Think about how you would define preparedness</strong></p>
<p>Preparedness can be defined as the readiness to take action, before, during and after a disaster. To be prepared therefore means to take precautionary measures before an imminent threat or disaster takes place and to help people and institutions respond to and cope with the effects. Disaster preparedness also means improving the quality and effectiveness of the existing community services in order to cope with any eventualities.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>A good state of preparedness can reduce the impact of disasters.</p>
<p>A greater number of lives and property can be saved in advance or within the first few hours of a disaster. With proper prior planning many problems of survival and health resulting from a disaster can be dealt with more efficiently.</p>
<p>The government has recommended the following strategies to be put in place for preparedness. They require a comprehensive assessment of risks and vulnerabilities in order to target potential disaster areas with management programmes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="national-contingency-plans">National Contingency Plans<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#national-contingency-plans" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The National Disaster Management Authority (NADIMA) has drawn up plans defining the actions to be taken to prevent and mitigate disasters as well as how to deal with preparedness, response and recovery. The contingency plans are as follows:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="response">Response<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#response" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the event of a disaster, the government, community and other partners will direct resources towards saving lives, property and environment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="recovery">Recovery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#recovery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The government in collaboration with development partners will put in place mechanisms to ensure fast recovery and reconstruction after a disaster.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="insurance-initiatives-in-response-and-recovery">Insurance Initiatives in Response and Recovery<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#insurance-initiatives-in-response-and-recovery" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Insurance firms are being encouraged to develop affordable products that can be made available to the society in order to underwrite some of the disaster related issues.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="strategic-food-reserves-and-stockpiles">Strategic Food Reserves and Stockpiles<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#strategic-food-reserves-and-stockpiles" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The government intends to strengthen maintenance of strategic food reserves and adequate stockpiles of other basic necessities required in the event of a disaster.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="the-disaster-trust-fund">The Disaster Trust Fund<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-disaster-trust-fund" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The establishment of a disaster fund to be managed by the National Disaster Management Authority, in order to facilitate immediate disaster response.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparing-the-community-for-disaster-management">Preparing the Community for Disaster Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparing-the-community-for-disaster-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>While going through the various units of this module, you should note that one of your responsibilities is not only to identify problems and create awareness about them, but also to promote community based primary health care, health education, immunisation and environmental improvement.</p>
<p>You are probably asking yourself the question "How are these related to the prevention or mitigation of disasters?" You will now look at this relationship.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="community-based-primary-health-care">Community Based Primary Health Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#community-based-primary-health-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You can encourage your community to set up disaster management support structures within the existing primary health care system. You can adopt a multi-disciplinary approach in which you enlist resource persons from the community or what is referred to as Community Own Resource Persons (CORPS).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="why-should-you-use-a-multidisciplinary-approach">Why Should You Use a Multidisciplinary Approach?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#why-should-you-use-a-multidisciplinary-approach" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is because each member brings along their specialised skills to mobilise community interest. These people can be called upon in the event of a disease outbreak, floods or other disaster.</p>
<p>Once you identify CORPS you need to obtain a consensus of opinion. This is very important so that you can harness the community's commitment to the proposed action.</p>
<p>As a supervisor and technical expert you should respect their views in order to woo them to respect your scientific input. This will enhance their participation in the recommendations which you have collectively made.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="health-education">Health Education<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#health-education" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should motivate and educate community members to adopt and sustain habits that reduce the risk of diseases and accidents. Your</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>health education should lay more emphasis on problem solving or action oriented efforts. You can help them to identify potential disasters that could happen and ask them to suggest how they can be managed and prevented. Remember to explain to them in simple ordinary terms and encourage them to share the information with others</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="immunisation">Immunisation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#immunisation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>From your past experience you will agree that respiratory and diarrhoeal diseases are major causes of morbidity and mortality in children. There are effective vaccines against the nine childhood immunisable diseases that manifest with respiratory and diarrhoeal disease complications.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nine-preventable-and-immunisable-childhood-diseases">Nine Preventable and Immunisable Childhood Diseases<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nine-preventable-and-immunisable-childhood-diseases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The nine preventable and immunisable childhood diseases include: poliomyelitis, mumps, diphtheria, tuberculosis, pertusis, measles, haemophilus influenza type b, hepatitis b and tetanus.</p>
<p>There are others that often flare up when the general body resistance is low or at times of disaster when hygiene becomes poor. They include typhoid fever, yellow fever, and influenza. Since in most cases only a small number of susceptible children are adequately immunised, there is always a danger of epidemics occurring from such infections. You should, therefore, work towards having high immunisation coverage in order to help the communities mitigate the effects of epidemics.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="environmental-improvement">Environmental Improvement<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#environmental-improvement" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are many improvements that a community can make to their environment in order to mitigate the effects of a disaster. These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Housing improvement</li>
<li>Good latrine construction</li>
<li>Protection of springs</li>
