<li>Improvement of food storage</li>
</ul>
<p>You have already covered how these can be improved in earlier units of this module. However, in the context of disaster management, housing improvement is important</p>
<p>in areas which are prone to landslides and earthquakes. You should point out that a permanent wall and floor helps to prevent the building from collapsing easily and reduces leakages and vermin. Construction and use of latrines is also important to curb disease outbreaks which are caused by poor excreta disposal. How about improvement of food storage?</p>
<p>You will have heard about the aflatoxin food poisoning that keeps recurring in the eastern province of Kenya due to poor storage of maize after harvest. As a community health nurse, you can team up with other experts to teach the community simple and affordable technologies which can help them prevent such disasters from taking place.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="emergency-response">Emergency Response<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#emergency-response" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>What is the usual reaction in the event of a catastrophe?</p>
<p>What psychological and emotional reactions occur in people?</p>
<p>You covered this in module one, unit two the section on adrenal glands. If you have forgotten you should go back and review it again.</p>
<p>When disaster strikes, the public reacts with terror and panic. Everybody is terrified and fearful for their safety and that of their family and friends. People tend to help themselves to safety before external help arrives. Panic is most common in crowded places, especially where there are no obvious exit points. Depending on the type of disaster at hand, some people may be buried in debris, as happened during the 1998 bomb blast, or cut off by floods.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="after-a-disaster-how-would-you-decide-which-victims-need-urgent-medical-attention">After a disaster how would you decide which victims need urgent medical attention?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#after-a-disaster-how-would-you-decide-which-victims-need-urgent-medical-attention" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When disasters happen the health facilities tend to be overwhelmed by casualties. It is easy to get confused and wonder who to attend to and who to keep waiting. Yet it is very important for you to make the right judgment in order to save lives. Fortunately, there is a process that is used to help in this. It is known as Triaging.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="concept-of-triaging">Concept of Triaging<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#concept-of-triaging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Triaging is a French term, coined into an English word. It originated from the army where injured soldiers were evacuated and methodically aligned for treatment.</p>
<p>Triaging is the evaluation and classification of casualties for purposes of treatment and</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>evacuation, so as to carry out resuscitation, emergency surgery or futility surgery (radical amputation) because of the severe results (intrinsic lethality) of the wounds. This means that through triaging you can establish priorities for treatment and evacuation during a disaster.</p>
<p>Triaging used to be a doctor's domain. However, due to advances in the nursing profession and the gradual expansion of our roles to provision of expert care, today more and more nurses have acquired triaging skills.</p>
<p>In any emergency situation, patients/victims/casualties are suddenly introduced into the emergency care system. You now have regular patients as well as victims of the disaster competing for your attention. Some of the regular cases may also be of an urgent nature. In order to manage this "chaos", you have to quickly create an organised flow of receiving and handling regular patients as well as emergency casualties. Often, the regular patients who do not have medical emergencies</p>
<p>usually comply when asked nicely to leave so that you can attend to the emergency cases.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="importance-of-creating-an-organised-flow">Importance of Creating an Organised Flow<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#importance-of-creating-an-organised-flow" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An organised flow shows that people know what they are doing. It instils confidence in both the workers and victims. The flow seeks to achieve the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Sets the tone and pace of the department</li>
<li>Assures the patient and their relatives or friends that their medical problems are being given priority regardless of the financial implications</li>
<li>Guards against denial of immediate care to anyone who requires it</li>
</ul>
<p>Colours are used in prioritising patients in a disaster scene according to their state and the urgency in which they require care.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 202 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="rapid-triage-in-multiple-patient-scenes">Rapid Triage in Multiple Patient Scenes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rapid-triage-in-multiple-patient-scenes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<table><thead><tr><th>Rapid Triage</th><th></th><th></th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>(for multiple patient scenes)</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Priority</td><td>Color</td><td>Condition</td><td>Notes</td></tr><tr><td>1</td><td>Red</td><td>Immediate</td><td>Life threatening</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>Yellow</td><td>Urgent</td><td>Can delay up to 1h</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>Green</td><td>Delayed</td><td>Up to 3 hours</td></tr><tr><td>4</td><td>Black</td><td>Deceased</td><td>No care needed.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="notes">Notes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#notes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Assessment of patients should be &lt; 1 minute each (Have someone else control bleeding during survey)</li>
<li>All unconscious patients are Priority 1 - Immediate</li>
<li>Walking wounded are usually Green - Priority 3</li>
<li>All pulseless patients are Black - Priority 4</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="mentation-loc-assessment">Mentation / LOC Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mentation-loc-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A - Alert: able to answer questions
V - Verbal: resoponds to verbal stimuli
P - Pain: responds only to pain stimuli. Protect airway
U - Unconscious: protect airway, consider intubation</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="goals-of-triaging">Goals of Triaging<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#goals-of-triaging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The goals of triaging are as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>Early patient assessment</li>
<li>Brief overall patient assessment</li>
<li>Determination of urgency of need of care</li>
<li>Implementation of the policy that the most critically ill patient receives priority</li>
<li>Documentation of the triage findings</li>
<li>Control of patient flow through the emergency department</li>
<li>Assignment of care area</li>
<li>Assignment of care provider</li>
<li>Initiation of diagnostic measures</li>
<li>Initiation of therapeutic measures</li>
<li>Infection control</li>
<li>Promotion of good public relations</li>
<li>Health education for patients and their families</li>
</ul>
<p>You will now look at what you should do to achieve some of these goals</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Priority 1 - Immediate transport:</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Unconscious, disorientated, very confused, rapid respirations, weak irregular pulse, severe uncontrolled bleeding, other signs of shock (cold, clammy skin, low blood pressure, etc)</td></tr><tr><td>Priority 2 - Urgent, can delay transport up to 1 hour:</td></tr><tr><td>Conscious, orientated, with any significant fracture or other significant injury, but without signs of shock.</td></tr><tr><td>Priority 3 - Delayed transport up to 3 hours:</td></tr><tr><td>Walking wounded, CAO x 3, minor injuries</td></tr><tr><td>Priority 4 - Deceased, no care needed:</td></tr><tr><td>No pulse, no respiration (open airway first), obvious mortal wounds (e.g. decapitation).</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="early-patient-assessment">Early Patient Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#early-patient-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You need to be flexible enough to adapt to the influx of patients. Spend at least four minutes and four seconds per patient. Although you are expected to be fast, you must be thorough while at the same time you strive to avoid creating a backlog of unserved patients in the waiting area. For a minimum assessment, you must at least do the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>Elicit the chief complaint</li>
<li>Perform a quick head to toe examination</li>
<li>Take the temperature, pulse, and BP</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="determining-urgency-of-need-of-care">Determining Urgency of Need of Care<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#determining-urgency-of-need-of-care" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should be able to determine who is to be seen first based on the urgency of the condition. In the Military, if severe casualties occur in conditions where transportation is difficult, casualties who are so severely injured that death seems imminent are placed in a delayed category. This may sound callous but after consideration you might see the sense in it.</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 203 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>However, following a disaster the most severe injuries and illness are generally taken in first regardless of the apparent prognosis of the emergency room or department.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="documentation-of-triage-findings">Documentation of Triage Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#documentation-of-triage-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Documentation in triaging is very important. Indeed if it is done carelessly it can even change your fate as a professional overnight! You should organise the record sheet/form such that there is space for triage notes in a conspicuous place. Remember that the time spent on important paper work can deny the patients precious time to be triaged. Even their relatives and friends get concerned if the patient stays too long in the triaging area before any treatment is started. You should therefore arrange to speed up this process because early documentation reduces time spent on diagnosis, treatment and discharge.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="triage-notes-are-your-primary-form-of-communication">Triage Notes are Your Primary Form of Communication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#triage-notes-are-your-primary-form-of-communication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Triage notes provide baseline data for the clinician who may care for the patient. Important decisions are based on this information. That is why you must ensure that they are factual, honest and informative.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assignment-of-care-providers">Assignment of Care Providers<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assignment-of-care-providers" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You should plan for the victim's next appointment with a specialist/physician. A physician can do this after ascertaining that the victim is not in immediate danger but requires review later. It can only be done when there is full documentation and the patient has given written informed consent. Usually it is the most senior/skilful health officer who oversees the assignment of duties in the areas of operation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="initiation-of-diagnostic-measures">Initiation of Diagnostic Measures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#initiation-of-diagnostic-measures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>If the number of patients is low, diagnostic measures can be put in place. Make sure that appropriate approved protocols are in use by all staff and are adhered to.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="qualities-and-qualifications-of-a-triageur">Qualities and Qualifications of a Triageur<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#qualities-and-qualifications-of-a-triageur" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A triageur has specific duties which they are expected to perform. In order to understand them, the following are the qualities and qualifications that a triageur is expected to have:</p>
<ul>
<li>A nursing practice license</li>
<li>At least six months experience in a general emergency unit in the recent past</li>
<li>Be physically and mentally healthy to meet the demands of the position</li>
<li>Broad knowledge of patient assessment and care</li>
<li>Ability to set priorities and determine urgency of need of care</li>
<li>Ability to function in stressful situations</li>
<li>Ability to relate to patients, families and co-workers without bias of any kind</li>
<li>Ability to promote good public relations</li>
<li>Knowledge, acceptance and adherence to legal aspects of triage</li>
<li>Ability to accept the responsibility inherent in the position</li>
<li>A good understanding of the philosophy and objectives of the institution, the emergency department and the triage system</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="duties-and-responsibilities-of-a-triageur">Duties and Responsibilities of a Triageur<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#duties-and-responsibilities-of-a-triageur" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are as follows:</p>
<ul>
<li>Assess all incoming patients within five minutes of arrival</li>
<li>Determine the urgency of need of care and assign urgency ratings</li>
<li>Designate the appropriate care areas and care providers</li>
<li>Document initial patient assessment</li>
<li>Measure and record initial signs wherever possible</li>
<li>Teach health care to patients, families as time allows</li>
<li>Take phone calls regarding incoming patients</li>
<li>Notify other care providers of incoming patients</li>
<li>Provide immediate care and seek assistance as necessary</li>
<li>Initiate diagnostic measures as indicated by protocol</li>
<li>Keep a log of unusual or noteworthy situations, that is, shootings, assaults or unidentified patients and report these situations to the appropriate persons</li>
<li>Control the flow of patients and visitors</li>
<li>Advise waiting families of the patient's progress if time allows</li>
<li>Obtain past history records if needed</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<ul>
<li>Maintain a balanced caseload in different care areas:
i) Maintain an awareness of care activity in the care area (for example cardio-pulmonary arrests, delays in care)
ii) Supervise clinical staff activities</li>
</ul>
<p>Although in the past any health personnel could be called upon to triage, it has become mandatory that triageurs receive medical education. Nurses of all levels with triaging skills are becoming more and more in demand. If you are an experienced emergency department nurse you may require a short in-service triage course. However, for large evacuations you will require a more intensive course.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="how-is-triaging-done">How is Triaging Done?<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#how-is-triaging-done" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Triaging involves what is known as subjective and objective assessment. That is, carrying out a patient diagnosis. You evaluate or assess the victim using medical knowledge to collect data and make decisions at the same time. As you will recall, one of the steps in patient diagnosis is the head to toe examination. This is done methodically so that you do not leave any part of the patient out. In triaging the acronym SOAP is used as a useful assessment guide.</p>
<p>It stands for:</p>
<p>S - Subjective assessment
O - Objective assessment
A - Assessment of clinical impressions/diagnosis
P - Plan of care</p>
<p>You will now consider the first two steps of this assessment guide in turn.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="subjective-assessment">Subjective Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#subjective-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the evaluation of a patient's illness and health history as the patient sees it. The data you collect is made up of what the patient remembers or the medical history that brought the patient to seek for care. Sometimes you may encounter patients who are hostile, delirious, confused, who do not speak or understand a common language, or are deaf. In this case you should get the information from a close relative or a friend who is agreeable to the victim and understands the victim well. In such a situation you must document the name of the informer and their relationship to the victim.</p>
<p>When carrying out a subjective assessment you should make sure you cover the following areas:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="history-of-present-illness-or-injury">History of Present Illness or Injury<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#history-of-present-illness-or-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This helps you to determine the urgency of need for care. Determine the chief complaint and write it in the patient's own words. Summarising what the patient says is often inaccurate and does not provide a good basis for evaluation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="duration-of-the-chief-complaint">Duration of the Chief Complaint<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#duration-of-the-chief-complaint" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>That is, for how long has this complaint been present?</p>
<p>Here, use calendar days or hours of the clock. They help to determine urgency of need for care or may help diagnosis of the disorder.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nature-of-chief-complaint">Nature of Chief Complaint<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nature-of-chief-complaint" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This helps to determine the cause of disease or urgency for need of care. You may choose to follow the systems of the body, that is, the nervous system, visual or auditory disturbances, respiratory, cardiovascular, and gastrointestinal.</p>
<p>The most significant symptoms are pain, abnormal bleeding, loss of function, weight loss/gain, fever, weakness or fatigue.</p>
<p>You could analyse each symptom using sub headings.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="analysing-symptoms-in-subjective-assessment">Analysing Symptoms in Subjective Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#analysing-symptoms-in-subjective-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You could analyse each symptom using the following sub headings:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="location">Location<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#location" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Be specific, ask the victim to point at the region of the symptom. Use the known names of the regions of the body including measurements if possible, for example, 2cm to the left of umbilicus. The regions of the body are: anterior, posterior, superior, inferior, medial, lateral, proximal, distal.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="onset">Onset<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#onset" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>You need to document whether it was abrupt or gradual or during an activity. What were the circumstances surrounding the onset, that is, what was going on at the time when the complaint was elicited?</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 206 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="timing">Timing<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#timing" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Does the event, for example pain, recur and at what intervals? What other activities are associated with it?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="character">Character<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#character" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Describe what the victim feels during the pain or event, for example, is the pain radiating, throbbing, tightness in the chest, breathlessness, and so on. Is the pain gnawing or tearing? Is it referred pain? Is there any discharges or abnormal stool?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="analysing-symptoms-in-subjective-assessment">Analysing Symptoms in Subjective Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#analysing-symptoms-in-subjective-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="intensity">Intensity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intensity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Does it interfere with the patient's activities of daily living? Does it prevent you from doing any activity? If so, then there is urgency for care, if not the person can be held at the back of the queue.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="aggravating-and-alleviating-factors">Aggravating and alleviating factors<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#aggravating-and-alleviating-factors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These too can help either to identify disease process or specific injuries. Is there anything that makes the symptoms better or worse?</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="associated-symptoms">Associated symptoms<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#associated-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are those that occur simultaneously, that is, bleeding, pain, dysfunction and so on.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pertinent-past-medical-history">Pertinent past medical history<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pertinent-past-medical-history" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This must be very brief that is why it is called "pertinent". You should note any chronic illness, surgery, hospitalisation or previous injury to same area.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="allergies">Allergies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#allergies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Record the name and nature of the drug.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="medication">Medication<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Record all current medications the victim may be taking including those that have been discontinued in the recent past. You should also record those that are taken on a regular basis. Record the name of drug, dosage and compliance.</p>
<p>Having looked at the subjective assessment, you will now move on to the objective assessment.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objective-assessment">Objective Assessment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objective-assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>This is what you, the triageur, measures and observes in the patient. Before you assess the victim, you should prepare a suitable venue. This should be a room as quiet as possible with no distraction for both the triageur and the patient so that you can both concentrate on the interview. It should be a one-on-one interview unless the patient is unable to express themselves. In this case a member of the family or close friend can do so on behalf of the patient. Before the interview you should, wherever possible, establish rapport and ensure patient's comfort.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="remember">Remember:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#remember" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="during-history-taking-use-simple-terms">During history taking use simple terms.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#during-history-taking-use-simple-terms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Before you finish with the victim summarise your notes aloud for the victim to hear. This helps to verify that their complaint has been heard and recorded correctly/accurately. Ask the victim to clarify what they mean by the expressions used so that you can add or delete as necessary.</p>
<p>As previously mentioned, the objective assessment of the patient is based on what you observe and measure in the victim. This falls under three categories:</p>
<ul>
<li>General appearance</li>
<li>Vital signs</li>
<li>Localised examination</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="general-appearance">General Appearance<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#general-appearance" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This calls for an experienced nurse/triageur. You assess the colour of the skin and mucus membranes, the temperature, hygiene and gait. You should also assess the level of consciousness and behaviour.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vital-signs">Vital Signs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vital-signs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Here, you check for:</p>
<ul>
<li>Temperature.</li>
<li>Heart rate.</li>
<li>Pulse for: rhythm, volume and rate.</li>
<li>Respiration: depth and rate.</li>
<li>Blood pressure for hypertension (mild, moderate, severe, accelerated, malignant) or hypotension. Hypertension is dangerous because it shows that the pressure is insufficient to perfuse the tissues of the body adequately. A previously hypertensive patient with a blood pressure of 200/140 can suffer from hypotension if it drops suddenly to</li>
</ul>
<p>normal 120/70. However, if the blood pressure of a patient who is warm, alert, active and making urine is 94/60, then this is absolutely normal. There is danger if a hypertensive victim develops tachycardia because this can be an indication of hypovolaemia. Such a victim should have blood pressure checked in both standing and sitting positions. It is important to rule out hypoadrenalism (Addison's disease) malnutrition, cachexia, chronic bed rest and neurologic disorders.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="localised-examination">Localised Examination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#localised-examination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Extensive physical exam is not required due to the semi private nature of the venue and emergency situation. Therefore, just examine the injured parts. X-rays are permissible if time and facilities allow. When assessing injuries, look out for the following:</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="injury-to-distal-limbs">Injury to Distal Limbs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#injury-to-distal-limbs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Observe for swelling, tenderness, obvious bone deformity, haematoma, ecchymosed type of movement, colour, temperature and neurological status. Document all the findings. There should be a room for immediate attention to obvious amputations as well as severe unstoppable haemorrhage.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="lacerations">Lacerations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lacerations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Deep major lacerations require immediate attention to avoid permanent functional difficulty and haemorrhage. You should therefore forward the victims to the physician. When assessing lacerations, you must record their location, length, depth, and if any vital structures are involved.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="burns">Burns<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#burns" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Use the "Rule of Nines" to estimate the body percentage of surface area. You have already covered this topic in module one, unit five, the section on management of critically ill patients. The other components you should describe when assessing burns include:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Surface area of the body</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Thickness of the tissues destroyed (that is, 1st, 2nd, and 3rd degree of burns)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Location of their burn</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pre existing health status of the patient</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Associated injuries</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-burns-and-resultant-tissue-injury">Types of Burns and Resultant Tissue Injury<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-burns-and-resultant-tissue-injury" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The table below will help you to identify the types of burns and resultant tissue injury.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Type of Burn</th><th>Skin layers involved</th><th>Appearance</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>First Degree</td><td>Superficial epidermis</td><td>Reddened</td></tr><tr><td>Second Degree</td><td>Partial skin thickness</td><td>Blisters</td></tr><tr><td>Third Degree</td><td>Full skin thickness</td><td>Dry hand</td></tr><tr><td>Charred</td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>In elastic</td><td></td><td></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="areas-of-the-body-that-present-with-special-problems-for-burn-victims">Areas of the Body that Present with Special Problems for Burn Victims<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#areas-of-the-body-that-present-with-special-problems-for-burn-victims" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The table below will help you identify the areas of the body that present with special debilitating problems for the victim in the future.</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Area</th><th>Problem</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Hands</td><td>Limit the patient's future ability to work</td></tr><tr><td>Face</td><td>Cosmetic reasons</td></tr><tr><td>Perineum</td><td>Problems with defecation, micturation, cleanliness</td></tr><tr><td>Feet</td><td>Immobilise the patient</td></tr><tr><td>Neck</td><td>May cause airway obstruction</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The danger of burns and especially those that cover a large surface area is loss of fluid and electrolytes. This is more serious in the young robust victim than older debilitated patient. Since you already covered burns in module one, unit five, you shall not go into details here again</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="eye-injuries">Eye Injuries<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#eye-injuries" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>These are important because of their location and sensitivity. You should have the visual acuity of the victim measured using the standard Snellen chart. Depending on your location when you are carrying out the assessment, measuring of visual acuity may be delayed if you do not have the chart near you. You should also look for foreign bodies if the victim has a penetrating wound. If you find a foreign body in the eye cover it with an eye shield and refer the victim immediately to an ophthalmologist. Hyphema or blood in the anterior chamber of the eye needs immediate care. Victims who present with this problem should be positioned with the head</p>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Bishop's Computers</p>
<p>angled at 40Â° and kept in a dark room. In the case of chemical burns you should irrigate the affected eye with one litre of normal sterile saline as soon as possible.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="illness">Illness<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#illness" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Be specific and look out for sore throat, earache, rashes, cellulites, abscess and document them accordingly.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="criteria-for-triage-decisions">Criteria for Triage Decisions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#criteria-for-triage-decisions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="documentation-in-triaging">Documentation in Triaging<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#documentation-in-triaging" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>When you were covering subjective and objective assessments in triaging, you looked at the importance of documenting your findings. But what is documentation in triaging? You shall now look at the meaning of documentation in triaging, its principles and some of the abbreviations you can use to refer to the common conditions.</p>
<p>A document in triaging is a brief and accurate patient record which uses an urgency rating in order to help you base your decisions for onward care. Your urgency rating establishes a baseline data on which other care decisions will be made.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="purpose-of-a-medical-record">Purpose of a Medical Record<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#purpose-of-a-medical-record" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The purpose of a medical record is to provide communication between members of the health care team. Such a record should therefore:</p>
<ul>
<li>Have complete and accurate data</li>
<li>Be written in clear concise terms</li>
<li>Be legible</li>
<li>Use an institutions protocol data collection tool</li>
<li>Use SOAP format to elicit both subjective and objective assessment information</li>
<li>Sign the document using full name and title, for example, H. Khamati, R.N., MBN</li>
<li>Indicate all the procedures you have carried out</li>
</ul>
<p>Bishop's Computers
Page 208 of 267
Bishop's Computers</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="common-abbreviations-and-symbols-used-in-triage">Common Abbreviations and Symbols Used in Triage<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#common-abbreviations-and-symbols-used-in-triage" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
